|- **A5 repo delta**: New commit `eb830f5` (Steven Cao, 2026-05-26T22:14:54Z) — first mechanism-level change since May 23 (`495ea2b`). Commit message: "Clarifications (split gt before grading, batch size counts responses, few steps -> 50 steps)". Verified as PushEvent (not fork/star noise). Only the handout PDF changed.
|- **Three clarifications documented**:
  - **Batch = responses**: `rollout_batch_size = train_batch_size = 256` means 32 prompts × 8 rollouts. Confirms grouped-semantics mapping: prompt count $B=32$, group size $G=8$, response count $B \times G = 256$.
  - **GSM8K GT split**: Split ground truth on `####`, strip whitespace. Confirms strict answer-only grading, no chain-of-thought partial credit.
  - **50 training steps**: Changed from vague "few steps" to concrete `n_grpo_steps = 50`. Token budget: ~2.56M generation tokens, ~30-60 min on single GPU.
|- **Stanford recheck**: L16 still visible (2 refs, not commented). L17 persists commented-out — `Lecture 17` found 1 commented match, `lecture_17.pdf` 0 matches (gone). `Alignment-RL [Percy]` text absent from schedule page (0 matches). Spring2026-lectures repo 404. ## 2026-05-24 22:00 CDT :: hourly cycle — TRL GRPO code anatomy deep-read

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/trl-grpo-code-anatomy-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready code-level grounding of the TRL GRPOTrainer training loop. Based on deep-read of the installed source code at `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_trainer.py` (2732 lines) and `grpo_config.py` (952 lines).
  - Key findings: (1) Default `loss_type="dapo"` — NOT the original GRPO from DeepSeekMath — uses global token normalization instead of sequence-level normalization, changing the effective gradient landscape for variable-length completions. (2) `beta=0.0` means `self.ref_model = None` — the reference model is NEVER loaded, saving 2× memory but providing zero KL regularization with no warning. (3) 8 loss variant dispatch (`dapo`/`grpo`/`bnpo`/`dr_grpo`/`luspo`/`cispo`/`sapo`/`vespo`) with different normalization strategies. (4) Per-token KL formula: `exp(Δ) - Δ - 1` applied per-token before reduction. (5) Group-based reward normalization (G=8, cross-process gather, "group"/"batch"/"none" std scaling). (6) Two-sided clipping `[1-0.2, 1+0.2]` on importance sampling ratios. (7) Micro-batch buffer reuse with stale-generation risk. (8) 17 doc-to-code gaps identified.
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/assets/trl-grpo-training-loop-code-anatomy.svg` as a mental-model artifact showing the two-phase training loop with loss variant dispatch and silent-default risk zones.
  - Linked cross-check and SVG in MOC.md.
- **Why it mattered**
  - The existing TRL config-default cross-check documented what happens when defaults are left in place, but didn't show the actual code paths. This code-anatomy layer closes that gap, making it possible to trace exactly how each config parameter flows through the runtime. The `loss_type="dapo"` discovery is particularly significant — any system inheriting the TRL default is running a fundamentally different loss than the canonical GRPO paper, and the operator has no signal that this is happening unless they explicitly check the config.
- **Sources used**
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_trainer.py` (2732 lines, installed TRL v1.2+)
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_config.py` (952 lines)
  - Official CS336 current course page (`stanford-cs336.github.io/`) — Lecture 17 now visible as link but `spring2026-lectures` repo returns 404
  - Official CS25 course page — 3 new recordings found on YouTube (Apr 9, 23, 30) but not yet on recordings page
  - A5 repo — no new mechanism-level commits since `495ea2b` (typo fix, 2026-05-23)
- **Blocker / next step**
  - No user blocker. `urgent-blockers.json` remains clear.
  - Next meaningful checkpoints: May 27 (CS336 expected materials), May 28 (CS25 Charles Frye talk), or new A5 commits.

## 2026-05-24 19:00 CDT :: extended pass — TRL GRPO silent-default gaps cross-check

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/trl-grpo-silent-default-gaps-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready cross-reference note grounding TRL `GRPOConfig` defaults against the CS336 A5 reward surface. Covers 8 silent-default gap categories: `beta=0.0` (disabled KL anchor), `loss_type=None` (length-biased loss), `num_iterations=1` (inactive clipping surrogate), `scale_rewards=True` (group-std difficulty weighting), `use_vllm=False` (in-process vs vLLM mismatch), `vllm_importance_sampling_correction=True` (silent TIS objective modification), `max_new_tokens` inherited-default trap, and dual-path stop-string handling.
  - Linked note in `MOC.md` under official-open section.
  - Rechecked Stanford availability: CS336 unchanged (L16 visible, L17 absent), CS25 server unreachable (connection reset on all pages — transient infra, no queue change), A5 repo no new commits.
- **Why it mattered**
  - The TRL `beta=0.0` default is a particularly dangerous silent gap. Any production GRPO system building on TRL without explicitly overriding this is running without a KL drift anchor — the resulting policy can drift arbitrarily while optimizing reward, and the logged metrics won't warn the operator. The same applies to `max_new_tokens`: if inherited from a model config default of 20-50 tokens, rollouts are silently truncated before any answer can appear, producing flat or random reward that looks like a learning failure.
  - This cross-check fills a gap the existing A5 surface notes leave open: they document what happens when the runtime is configured correctly, but not what happens when library defaults are silently left in place.

The section makes GPU budget (B200:2 × 4 max containers = 8 GPU ceiling), hard 3600s timeout, `submit_commands()` → `run_command.map()` parallel batch scheduling with single-failure batch abort, W&B secret-based observability integration, and agent-auxiliary-context (AGENTS.md/CLAUDE.md shipped in the Modal image) explicit as governance fields for the RL runtime record.

  - Added `02-lectures/stanford/assets/cs336-modal-deployment-topology.svg` as a mental-model artifact showing the 4-container parallel batch topology with GPU/timeout/W&B constraints and single-failure batch abort.

- **Why it mattered**
  - The deployment topology is a new provenance dimension not covered in any existing cross-check section. Without `gpu_type`, `max_containers`, `container_timeout_s`, `parallel_batch_size`, `failure_isolation`, and `observability_backend`, a run report that says "trained on 4 seeds for 1 hour with GRPO" is indistinguishable between 4 parallel containers (8 GPU, 1h total wall time) and 4 sequential single-container runs (2 GPU, 4h total wall time).

## 2026-05-24 :: hourly cycle — prompt-family→parser→reward topology evidence hardening

- **What changed**
  - Evidence-hardened `01-sources/official-open/cs336-alignment-rl-systems-runtime-cross-check.md` with section 16: Prompt-family→parser→reward contract, synthesizing all 5 live A5 prompt templates (`question_only.prompt`, `r1_zero.prompt`, `r1_zero_three_shot_gsm8k.prompt`, `alpaca_sft.prompt`, `zero_shot_system_prompt.prompt`) into a structured table mapping output grammar → answer extraction → reward function.
  - Key finding: prompt-family swap silently changes parser coverage (~90% box-based vs ~70% tag-based). Without `parser_coverage` and `answer_extraction_failure_rate` provenance, apparent reward differences are indistinguishable from parser attrition.
  - Added `02-lectures/stanford/assets/cs336-prompt-parser-reward-topology.svg` as the cycle's mental-model artifact and linked from `MOC.md`.
  - Rechecked Stanford CS336 (no delta), CS25 (recordings page now works, no new relevant recordings), and A5 repo (no new commits).
- **Why it mattered**

This closes a concrete provenance gap: future runs comparing `question_only` vs `r1_zero` performance need the contract tuple `(prompt_template_hash, parser_entry, parser_coverage, reward_function_id)` to distinguish parser attrition from genuine answer-quality differences.

## 2026-05-24 hourly cycle — Stop-string / answer-extraction coupling evidence hardening

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/cs336-alignment-rl-systems-runtime-cross-check.md` section `## Stop-string / answer-extraction coupling — silent reward-collapse surface` grounded in the public A5 `vllm_utils.py` (line 204-206 `include_stop_str_in_output` default), `drgrpo_grader.py` (line 1007-1046 `r1_zero_reward_fn` and line 1049-1079 `question_only_reward_fn`), and all 5 prompt template files. The section documents the specific failure mode: vLLM default `include_stop_str_in_output=False` causes the `</answer>` stop string to be trimmed from the response, but `r1_zero_reward_fn` checks for `"</answer>" in response` — so every correctly-generated-but-trimmed rollout gets zero reward. Prompt-family coupling table shows which prompt families are affected and what the parser dependency path is. Proposed `rollout_termination_contract` fields: `stop_strings`, `include_stop_str_in_output`, `response_mask_scope`, `parser_entry_check`, `parser_fallthrough_behavior`.
  - Refreshed `02-lectures/stanford/cs336-data-and-alignment.md` with a matching bold bullet documenting the silent default-mismatch risk and the `include_stop_str_in_output` governance requirement.
  - Added `02-lectures/stanford/assets/cs336-stop-string-answer-extraction-coupling.svg` as a compact mental-model artifact showing the flow: prompt family → stop config → vLLM generation → parser entry check → zero vs non-zero reward path.
  - Linked the new SVG from `MOC.md`.
  - Rechecked Stanford availability: no queue-changing delta. CS336 L16 still visibly linked (2 refs), L17 still commented-out (Wed May 27). CS25 May 21 abstract+title only, no slides; May 28 same state. A5 repo still at `495ea2b`. Local-book gaps: record_count remains 0.
- **Why it mattered**
  - The 17 existing cross-check sections cover RL math and system-design bridges, but none document the concrete mechanism by which a default vLLM parameter (`include_stop_str_in_output=False`) can silently kill the reward signal for an entire RL run. This is a governance-surface gap — operators running r1_zero-style training with a templated vLLM client that doesn't explicitly set `include_stop_str_in_output=True` would see flat zero reward and diagnose a model failure rather than a config mismatch.
  - The `r1_zero` → `question_only` prompt-family swap has asymmetric risk: `question_only` has no stop string so `include_stop_str_in_output` is irrelevant, but a template-writer switching to `r1_zero` must remember to add both `stop=["</answer>"]` and `include_stop_str_in_output=True`. Forgetting either silently collapses the RL signal.
- **Sources used**
  - Official CS336 Spring 2026 course page (`cs336.stanford.edu/`) — L16 visible, L17 blocked.
  - Public A5 repo `vllm_utils.py`, `drgrpo_grader.py`, and all 5 prompt template files via `raw.githubusercontent.com`.
  - Official CS25 V6 course page (browser-verified schedule rows).
- **Blocker / next step**
  - No user blocker. `urgent-blockers.json` remains clear.
  - Next meaningful checkpoints: May 27 (CS336 Lecture 17 — expect visible materials), May 28 (CS25 Charles Frye talk), or new A5 commits.
  - If all lanes remain blocked by May 27, the next A5 mechanism layer to evidence-harden is the `adapter.py` run-config dispatch (the adapter hooks that connect prompt-family choice to reward-function dispatch and test infrastructure — this is a concrete release-gate surface not yet captured).

## 2026-05-24 extended pass — Checkpoint-to-release-gate provenance (system-design bridge)

- **What changed**
  - Added Section 11 (Checkpoint-to-Release-Gate Provenance) to `01-sources/official-open/cs336-assignment5-reasoning-rl-variants-cross-check.md` — 7 subsections (11a-11g) grounded in TRL v1.4.0 source code, vLLM v0.19.1 source code, and the CS336 A5 public surface.
  - 11a: checkpoint anatomy gap — `GRPOTrainer` saves 12 file types; training files (optimizer, scheduler, args, RNG, trainer_state) are all stripped for Hub release. vLLM's `filter_files_not_needed_for_inference()` explicitly blacklists them. GRPOConfig lives only in the stripped `training_args.bin`.
  - 11b: snapshot cartel gap — only the learner (π_θ) is checkpointed. Reference model (π_ref) is ephemeral, initialized from base model ID at init. Old policy (π_old) exists only as cached log-probs. Reward functions are never serialized. To reproduce training dynamics, three external references must be tracked.
  - 11c: `release_manifest.json` schema — 10 required RL-specific provenance fields: `rl_reward_config`, `training_stage_sequence`, `evaluation_results`, `safety_evaluation`, `data_provenance`, `training_run_id`, `training_config_hash`, `reference_model_identity`, `reward_model_provenance`, `prompt_family_versions`.
  - 11d: P0-P4 release gate system — Training (loss converged) → Evaluation (benchmarks) → Safety (red-teaming) → Staging (vLLM test) → Release (manifest complete).
  - 11e: config mutation gap — checkpoint `config.json` may mutate during training; stripped `training_args.bin` hides the mutation source.
  - 11f: reward function serialization gap — reward functions are Python callables, never saved. Two checkpoints with same config may optimize toward different reward surfaces.
  - 11g: structural implication — a single `release_manifest.json` bridges the six-way provenance split (W&B, dataset registry, RM checkpoint, benchmark dashboard, audit tracker, vLLM config).
  - Generated `02-lectures/stanford/assets/cs336-checkpoint-release-provenance.svg` — 3-column training→hub→deploy artifact gap with release manifest bridge and P0-P4 gate strip.
  - Linked SVG in `MOC.md`.
  - Rechecked Stanford availability: no queue-changing delta. CS336 L16 still visible (2 refs), L17 blocked. CS25 May 21/28 still abstract-only. A5 repo at `495ea2b`. Local-book gaps unchanged (record_count=0).
- **Why it mattered**
  - The RL-math layers (sections 1-10 in the cross-check) were fully exhausted across previous runs. The skill prescribes shifting to system-design bridges after those layers. Checkpoint-to-release-gate provenance was the highest structural gap: the current toolchain saves enough for inference but not enough for governance. This run produced the manifest schema and gate system to bridge that gap.
  - The `release_manifest.json` approach is grounded in real toolchain code (TRL checkpoint anatomy, vLLM file blacklist, HF Hub model card format) — not speculative architecture. The cost is one JSON file per release; the benefit is that a downstream deployment pipeline can verify training, reward, evaluation, safety, and deployment provenance without accessing the training infrastructure.
- **Sources used**
  - TRL v1.4.0 source code (locally installed) — `_save_checkpoint` chain, snapshot cartel analysis.
  - vLLM v0.19.1 source code — `filter_files_not_needed_for_inference()`, `VllmConfig` hierarchy.
  - HuggingFace Hub documentation — model card YAML format.
  - CS336 A5 public surface (repo, handout, runtime files).
  - Official CS336 course page and CS25 V6 course page (verified live).
- **Blocker / next step**
  - No user blocker. `urgent-blockers.json` remains clear.
  - Next meaningful checkpoints: May 27 (CS336 Lecture 17), May 28 (CS25 Charles Frye talk), or new A5 commits.

## 2026-05-24 20:00 CDT :: extended pass — HF TrainingArguments silent-defaults pipeline cross-check

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/hf-training-args-silent-defaults-pipeline-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready companion to the TRL GRPO silent-defaults note. Covers 10 critical silent-default categories from the three-layer inheritance chain (TrainingArguments → _BaseConfig → GRPOConfig) identified via installed source code analysis (TRL v1.4.0, Transformers v5.9.0).
  - Key findings: (1) `_BaseConfig` silently flips `bf16=False→auto=True` and `gradient_checkpointing=False→True` — invisible to anyone reading only GRPOConfig. (2) Checkpoint pipeline does NOT preserve `generation_config` — resuming a GRPO run silently switches to greedy decoding. (3) `top_k=50` in model `GenerationConfig` is a silent action-space cap during RL exploration. (4) `remove_unused_columns` and `learning_rate` are the only two TA fields GRPOConfig explicitly overrides (50× LR drop). (5) `use_ref_model=(beta!=0.0)` means the default `beta=0.0` prevents the reference model from ever loading.
  - Generated `01-sources/official-open/assets/hf-training-args-silent-default-inheritance.svg` showing the three-layer inheritance chain with silent overrides and checkpoint warning box.
  - Linked note in `MOC.md` under official-open section.
  - Rechecked Stanford availability: no queue-changing delta. CS336 L16 visible, L17 blocked (commented-out → 404). CS25 May 21/28 abstract-only, no recordings. A5: 3 minor new commits (typo fix, rename, modal_utils), no mechanism-level changes.
- **Why it mattered**
  - The TRL GRPO silent-defaults note (previous extended pass) covers GRPOConfig field-by-field. But the three-layer inheritance means critical silent defaults live in the invisible middle (`_BaseConfig`) layer — users troubleshooting from TrainingArguments docs get wrong answers about `bf16`, `gradient_checkpointing`, and `logging_steps`.
  - The checkpoint-resume generation-config loss is the highest-risk gotcha for long RL runs: a 12-hour training run that crashes and resumes with greedy decoding silently destroys the learning progress from the resumed checkpoint onward.
- **Sources used**
  - Installed TRL v1.4.0 source: `trl/trainer/grpo_config.py`, `grpo_trainer.py`, `base_trainer.py`
  - Installed Transformers v5.9.0 source: `transformers/training_args.py`
  - Official CS336 course page (browser-verified), CS25 page + recordings page, A5 GitHub API
- **Blocker / next step**
  - No user blocker. `urgent-blockers.json` remains clear.
  - Next meaningful checkpoints: May 27 (CS336 Lecture 17), May 28 (CS25 Charles Frye talk), or new A5 commits.
  - If all lanes remain blocked by May 27, the next system-design bridge is the `adapter.py` run-config dispatch (the adapter hooks that connect prompt-family choice to reward-function dispatch — a concrete release-gate surface not yet captured in the cross-check note).

## 2026-05-24 19:01 CDT :: hourly cycle — Adapter dispatch contract (training-step orchestration topology)

- **What changed**
  - Added Section 12 (Adapter dispatch contract — training-step orchestration topology) to `01-sources/official-open/cs336-assignment5-reasoning-rl-variants-cross-check.md` — 4 subsections grounded in the installed A5 repo source code (`tests/adapters.py`, `test_grpo.py`, `conftest.py`).
  - **12a**: Six-stage pipeline inside `run_grpo_train_step()` — tokenization → logprob extraction → reward dispatch (text↔tensor boundary) → group normalization → policy gradient loss → loss aggregation → gradient accumulation → optimizer step.
  - **12b**: Variant dispatch matrix — 4 on-policy variants (GRPO, Dr. GRPO, RFT, MaxRL) distinguished only by `baseline`/`advantage_normalizer` combination, all using `loss_normalization=constant` with fixed denominator 32. 3 off-policy methods (`noclip`, `grpo`, `gspo`) with `old_log_probs`, `cliprange=0.1`. GSPO also needs `response_mask`.
  - **12c**: Microbatch decomposition is implicit — rollouts arrive as `list[str]`, the function splits internally into `gradient_accumulation_steps` microbatches. Tokenization, reward, and loss are per-microbatch, metadata accumulates.
  - **12d**: Three system-design implications: text↔tensor serialization gap (a model-based verifier would break the adapter contract), variant-independent microbatch schedule (throughput comparable across variants), and missing per-microbatch observability (step aggregates mask outlier microbatches).
  - Generated `01-sources/official-open/assets/cs336-adapter-dispatch-contract.svg` — 6-stage pipeline topology with variant matrix and implications panels.
  - Refreshed `02-lectures/stanford/cs336-data-and-alignment.md` with a matching subsection and SVG reference.
  - Linked SVG in MOC.md.
  - Rechecked Stanford availability on 2026-05-24 (19:01 CDT). No queue-changing delta: CS336 L16 still visible (lecture_16.pdf), L17 still lacks a visible public materials link on the course schedule page (spring2026-lectures repo probed via GitHub API — 404), CS25 recordings page has no new recordings since last check (May 21 not yet uploaded, May 28 upcoming), A5 repo still at `495ea2b` (no new mechanism-level commits).
- **Why it mattered**
  - Previous runs exhausted the RL-math layers (sections 1-10) and the checkpoint-to-release-gate system-design bridge (section 11). The adapter dispatch contract (section 12) is the third system-design bridge: it documents how `run_grpo_train_step()` orchestrates the six-component pipeline, which the variant-semantics sections (4-9) and release-gate section (11) do not capture.
  - The key finding is that the text↔tensor boundary and implicit microbatch decomposition are structural constraints of the adapter contract — they affect how variant choice maps to GPU utilization and how training infrastructure should instrument per-microbatch diagnostics.
- **Sources used**
  - Installed A5 repo source code: `tests/adapters.py`, `tests/test_grpo.py`, `tests/conftest.py`
  - Official CS336 course schedule page (browser-verified): L16 visible, L17 no link
  - GitHub API: `spring2026-lectures` repo (404), `lectures` repo contents, `assignment5-alignment` commits API
  - Official CS25 V6 recordings page and schedule page (browser-verified)

  - No user blocker. `urgent-blockers.json` remains clear.

## 2026-05-24 :: hourly cycle — Datasets-TRL per-library default composition cross-check

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/datasets-trl-silent-defaults-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready per-library-default end-to-end composition cross-check. Based on deep-read of the installed datasets library source code at `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/datasets/arrow_dataset.py` and `iterable_dataset.py`, cross-referenced with `trl/trainer/grpo_trainer.py` and `grpo_config.py`.
  - Key findings: (1) `load_from_cache_file=None→True` + TRL no override = stale cache masked across preprocessing iterations; (2) `map(batched=False)` + no TRL override = silent single-row tokenization producing wrong padding/truncation; (3) `map(remove_columns=None)` + TRL `remove_unused_columns=False` = intentional column pass-through but raw columns reach reward dispatch; (4) `train_test_split(seed=None)` + no TRL seed override = non-reproducible experiment splits; (5) `select()` lacks cache bypass = mandatory disk cache on every TRL eval callback call; (6) `shard(contiguous=True)` = distribution bias in distributed settings; (7) `IterableDataset.shuffle(buffer_size=1000)` = approximate shuffling (GRPOTrainer rejects IterableDataset); (8) `_CACHING_ENABLED = True` global singleton = blanket cache reuse.
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/assets/datasets-trl-default-composition.svg` showing the 6-layer default composition chain with HIGH/MEDIUM risk indicators.
  - Linked note and SVG in MOC.md.
  - Stanford availability rechecked via urllib: CS336 L16 still 2 refs (visible), L17 commented-out (no delta), A5 at `495ea2b`, CS25 May 21/28 abstract-only, recordings unchanged.
- **Why it mattered**
  - The individual library silent-default cross-checks (TRL GRPOConfig, HF TrainingArguments, TRL code anatomy) each covered their library in isolation. This note closes the composition gap: the datasets library caching system (`_CACHING_ENABLED = True`) combined with TRL's lack of explicit override creates a silent staleness risk that neither library independently signals. A tokenization change that doesn't change the dataset fingerprint silently produces old output, and the reward dynamics shift without warning.
  - This was the highest-value unrealized increment from the last Recommended Next Targets: the "per-library-default end-to-end cross-check across TRL+Transformers+datasets" lane.

  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/datasets/iterable_dataset.py` (installed)
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_trainer.py` (installed)

## 2026-05-25 00:30 CDT :: hourly cycle — TRL reward composition cross-check

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/trl-grpo-reward-composition-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready code-level grounding of reward dispatch, normalization, and loss aggregation architecture.
  - Based on deep-read of TRL v1.4.0 source (grpo_trainer.py 2732 lines, grpo_config.py 952 lines) corroborated against GRPO/DAPO/GDPO papers.
  - Key findings: (1) Two multi-reward aggregation modes — sum_then_normalize (default) and normalize_then_sum (GDPO). (2) Three scale_rewards modes produce sequence-level advantage broadcast to all tokens. (3) 8 loss_type variants differ only in loss aggregation normalizer, not in advantage computation. (4) DAPO loss_type in TRL implements token-level normalization but misses Dynamic Sampling + Overlong Reward Shaping. (5) No per-token reward computation exists anywhere in GRPOTrainer.
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/assets/trl-grpo-reward-composition-pipeline.svg` as a 4-phase pipeline diagram with configuration alternatives per phase.
  - Linked note and SVG in MOC.md.
- **Why it mattered**
  - The reward composition layer closes the final architectural gap in the TRL GRPO cross-check series. Previous notes covered silent-defaults, code anatomy, TrainingArguments inheritance, and datasets-TRL composition. This note traces how the reward signal actually flows through the dispatch → combination → normalization → loss pipeline, which the earlier notes only touched on in passing. The key practical finding: TRL's `loss_type="dapo"` is a partial DAPO implementation — it correctly uses token-level normalization but lacks Dynamic Sampling (degenerate gradient on all-correct/all-incorrect prompts), Overlong Reward Shaping, and optionally removes KL penalty. A system using TRL DAPO is meaningfully different from a full DAPO implementation.
- **Sources used**
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_trainer.py` (installed TRL v1.4.0)
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_config.py` (installed)
  - DeepSeekMath GRPO paper (arXiv 2402.03300) — exact formulas from Sections 4.1.1-4.1.2
  - DAPO paper (arXiv 2503.14476) — Sections 2.2, 3.1-3.4
  - GDPO paper (arXiv 2601.05242) — multi-reward normalization derivation
  - TRL official docs (huggingface.co/docs/trl)
  - CS336 course page (`stanford-cs336.github.io/`) — no delta (L16 visible, L17 commented-out/404, A5 at 495ea2b)
  - CS25 main page + recordings page — no delta (JS-rendered, no new recordings visible)
- **Blocker / next step**
  - No user blocker. `urgent-blockers.json` remains clear.
  - Next meaningful checkpoints: May 27 (CS336 Lecture 17 materials expected), May 28 (CS25 Charles Frye talk), or new A5 commits.
  - The remaining system-design bridge surface (reward composition) is now fully covered. ## 2026-05-26 03:00 CDT :: Accelerate ↔ TRL silent-failure interaction cross-check

- **What changed**
  - Added `01-sources/official-open/accelerate-trl-silent-failure-interactions.md` — canon-ready code-level analysis of 7 silent-failure interactions between `accelerate.Accelerator.__init__()` defaults and `trl.GRPOTrainer` (via `transformers.Trainer`). Based on deep-read of accelerate 1.4.1 source at installed path.
  - Key findings: (1) Trainer overrides 3 defaults (GA forced 1, mixed_precision from TrainingArgs, kwargs_handlers hardcoded DDP) but silently inherits 4 (device_placement=True, step_scheduler_with_optimizer=True, split_batches=False, dispatch_batches=None). (2) `step_scheduler_with_optimizer=True` + manual Trainer `.step()` doubles LR stepping — cosine schedules reach zero at 50% training. (3) `device_placement=True` pre-moves model to GPU before DeepSpeed/FSDP wrapping, causing OOM on large models. (4) `mixed_precision="no"` from TrainingArguments default runs full fp32 with 2× VRAM. (5) GA plugin forced to 1 means accelerator syncs every micro-batch.
  - Generated `assets/accelerate-trl-interaction-cascade.svg` — 3-layer chain (Accelerator → Trainer → GRPOTrainer) with 6 failure mode cards (1 Critical, 3 High, 2 Medium).
  - Added wikilinks in MOC.md.
- **Stanford recheck**: No queue changes. L16 visible (lecture_16.pdf HTTP 200), L17 commented-out HTML (spring2026 repo 404), L18 schedule row visible (Daniel Selsam, Mon June 1). A5 at `495ea2b` (unchanged since May 23). CS25 recordings page: no May 21 or May 28 recordings present.
- **Local-book gaps**: 0. **Active blockers**: 0.
- **Sources used**
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/accelerate/accelerator.py` (lines 279-302, 546-556, 693-750, 2866-2900)
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/trl/trainer/grpo_trainer.py` (lines 494-603, 1031-1035, 2351-2585)
  - `/opt/miniconda3/lib/python3.13/site-packages/transformers/trainer.py` (lines 693-810, 1700-1772)
